Introduction
The Louisiana State Government Telephone Directory is divided into four sections:
The Information Section contains information concerning long distance dialing. It also
contains a quick reference telephone list for access to key personnel and major sections at
the Office of Technology Services Network Services (OTS Network Services).
The Listings Section contains telephone numbers for state agencies. These listings are
arranged alphabetically by city and agency. Local dialing instructions can be found before
the listings of each of the seven major metropolitan areas.
The Reference Section contains Executive Branch elected and appointed officials, telephone
numbers for Louisiana’s congressional delegation, state legislators, and a list of Louisiana
colleges and universities.
The Telecommunications Coordinators Section explains the responsibilities of a state
agency Telecommunications Coordinator.
The Louisiana State Government Telephone Directory is published by OTS Network Services
in an effort to provide an accurate, effective source of information to state agencies. The ability
to provide correct information to state agencies, as well as to the general public, is directly
related to the quality of telephone directory information furnished by state agencies. If
corrections to any listing are necessary, please follow the procedures outlined in the
Telecommunications Coordinators Section under “Directory Listings Changes.”
The Louisiana State Government Telephone Directory is published on the web at
www.doa.la.gov/OTS/OTM/listings/sgtd.pdf.
Any suggestions or ideas for enhancements to the directory may be forwarded to the OTS
Network Services Information and Training Section using the survey included in the front of
the directory.
For additional information about OTS Network Services,
www.doa.la.gov/Pages/ots/Telecommunications/index.aspx.

State Government Directory Assistance
Please consult your State Government Telephone Directory before placing any calls to public
assistance operators for state government listings as directory assistance calls are billable.
If you are experiencing a problem reaching a number in this directory or if you require help in
obtaining a state number not listed in this directory, contact the state government operators
at one of the numbers listed below.
BATON ROUGE ........... 225 342-6600
STATEWIDE ................ 800 256-7777

Long Distance Calls
Under this dial plan, authorized long distance users place long distance calls by dialing “1”
then the area code and seven digit telephone number. Each agency is billed monthly for its
actual usage.

International Calls
To make business related international calls, the telephone must be unrestricted for
international calling. Then—
• From an unrestricted AT&T Centrex station—
• Dial 9 for an outside line then dial 0 + 11, the country code, city code, and the local number.
• From a unrestricted PBX station—
• Obtain an outside line then dial 0 + 11, the country code, city code, and the local number.
• From an unrestricted business line or trunk—
• Dial 0 + 11, the country code, city code, and the local number.

3

State Government Dialing Instructions
State AT&T Centrex Service Users—
Major Metropolitan Abbreviated Dialing
• To reach another local State Government number with the same prefix, dial a designated
code + last four digits.
• To reach a local non-state number dial 9 + seven digit telephone number.
• Dialing instructions are included before each of the major metropolitan areas listed in this
directory. If further assistance is needed, contact the OTS Network Services System Projects
Manager at 225 342-1419 to obtain the appropriate codes.
To make business related long distance calls anywhere in the Continental U.S. from an
authorized station, dial “1” + area code + seven digit telephone number.
To place a toll free (800/888/877/866/855) call:
• Dial 9 + toll free number
Other State Centrex Users—
• Contact your agency’s Telecommunications Coordinator for feature and dialing instructions.
State PBX Users—
• Contact your System Administrator for feature and dialing instructions.

4

Louisiana Relay Service
Louisiana Relay Service (711, or 800 846-5277 for TTY/TDD users or 800 947-5277 for voice
users) is a 24-hour service that provides telephone communication between people who are
deaf, hard of hearing, deaf-blind or speech disabled, through the use of specialized equipment
to communicate freely with people who use a standard telephone.
During a relay call, an operator or communications assistant will voice everything typed by the
TTY/TDD user and type everything said by the telephone user. In this way, the relay allows
people who are deaf, hard of hearing or speech disabled to have a telephone conversation with
anyone, anytime, even if the other person does not have special equipment. For more
information on this or other Louisiana Relay Services and internet relay calling, visit their
website at www.hamilton.net/relay/la.

Using Voice Messaging Service
Voice Messaging Service (VMS) is a technology that can help you perform your job more
effectively. It can minimize the problems associated with telephone tag, unanswered
telephones, and the taking and distribution of internal messages. VMS answers calls, makes
messages immediately available to the person called, and captures and delivers the complete
message including the tone and mood of the caller.
For Your Personal Greetings—
• Be natural—Let your greeting reflect your personality. Be pleasant and friendly; the smile
you record with your voice will be heard by your caller. Listen to your greeting and hear
what the caller will hear; is it OK?
• Be distinct—Speak clearly and loudly enough for the caller to hear and understand your
greeting. Don't ramble or detract from your greeting with “ums” and pauses. Unwanted
background noise will be recorded with your greeting; so, make sure things are quiet while
recording.
• Include main points—Tell the caller your name, department or agency affiliation, if you are
in the office or not, and a time frame for your reply.
• Update your greeting—Change your greeting to reflect your daily schedule and keep callers
up to date. Include instructions on how to use the system, especially those for how to reach a
person.
• Check your messages frequently—Check for messages frequently. Be sure to act upon your
messages and return calls. This leads to callers' positive acceptance of the technology and
enables you to be more effective and provide better customer service.

Repair and Trouble Reporting
In an effort to provide practicable operating telephone systems, OTS Network Services relies
on state agencies to report telephone system problems. The following steps should be followed
when experiencing a problem:
• Try to place the call or activate the feature a second time.
• Then, try to determine if the problem is in the telephone or in the telephone line or jack.
With a plug-in telephone, unplug the telephone and cord and try a known working telephone
and cord in the same jack. If the second telephone works properly, the problem may be with
the telephone instrument. If the second telephone does not work properly, the problem may
be with the telephone line or jack.
• After attempting to determine whether the problem is with the instrument or the line or jack,
report this information to your agency Telecommunications Coordinator.
Your
Telecommunications Coordinator will report your problem to the OTS Network Services Help
Desk for resolution.

ABBREVIATED DIALING INSTRUCTIONS FOR BATON ROUGE
If you are dialing from a Baton Rouge state government number, you may be able to use abbreviated dialing to reach another local state government telephone
number. Using the chart below, dial the one digit code + the last 4 digits of the desired telephone number. If no code is listed, dial 9 + the 7 digit telephone
number. For all other local numbers, dial 9 + the 7 digit telephone number.

ABBREVIATED DIALING FOR NEW ORLEANS

361

If you are dialing from a New Orleans state government number, you may be able to use abbreviated dialing to reach another local telephone number.
Using the chart below, dial the one digit code + the last 4 digits of the desired telephone number. If no code is listed, dial 9 + the 7 digit telephone number.
For all other local numbers, dial 9 + the 7 digit telephone number.

SHREVEPORT (318)
Abbreviated Dialing—If you are dialing from a 676 Shreveport state government
number you can dial 3 + the last 4 digits of the desired telephone number to reach any
other 676 Shreveport state government number. If you are dialing from a 862 or 869
Shreveport state government number you can dial 3 + the last 4 digits of the desired
telephone number to reach any other 862 or 869 Shreveport state government
number. For all other local numbers dial 9 + the 7 digit telephone number.

Telecommunications Coordinators
All state agencies shall appoint one or more representatives to be designated as the agency
Telecommunications Coordinator(s). The Telecommunications Coordinator is recognized by the
Office of Technology Services Network Services (OTS NS, formerly OTM) as the agency’s
authorized representative for approving telecommunications matters, including service orders
and expenditures, resulting from authorized agency telecommunications activity.
A list of current Telecommunications Coordinators for state agencies can be found on the OTS
website at www.doa.la.gov/Pages/ots/Index.aspx.

Service Requests for Existing Systems
All requests for changes to existing telecommunications services and equipment must be
submitted by your Telecommunications Coordinator to the OTS Network Services as soon as a
need is known or anticipated. Requests must be submitted on the Communications Services
Request Form (Form OTM/S-8) which may be obtained from the OTS website at
www.doa.la.gov/Pages/ots/Index.aspx or by calling Customer Service at 225 342-7720.
If additional information about telecommunications services and equipment is needed, please
contact your agency's Telecommunications Coordinator.

Acquisition of Telecommunications Systems
The Office of Technology Services Network Services (formerly the Office of Telecommunications
Management or OTM) is responsible for assisting in identifying telecommunications needs and
formulating procedures for acquiring telecommunications systems for state agencies. Agencies
planning new facilities, relocations or renovations should notify Project Requests at the Office
of Technology Services Network Services, Post Office Box 94280, Baton Rouge, Louisiana
70804-9280 or call 225 342-7720.
Agencies experiencing severe or recurring problems with existing systems may submit a letter
requesting a complete system evaluation to the Assistant Administrator of Communications
Services and Support at the above address. If it is determined that an existing system is
inadequate or that a new system is required, OTS Network Services will assist the agency in
procuring an appropriate system in accordance with state procurement procedures.

88

Telecommunications Charges
The Office of Technology Services Network Services (OTS NS) is responsible for coordinating
the payment of all telecommunications costs incurred by agencies and provides for equitable
billing to agencies for telecommunications services utilized.
All telecommunications systems and services are assigned a cost center for billing purposes.
Telecommunications Coordinators are responsible for obtaining the proper account codes from
departmental fiscal offices to insure charges are being applied correctly. OTS NS must be
notified in writing by the Telecommunications Coordinator when an agency's cost center or
billing address is to be changed.
State agencies should review and audit monthly invoices for billing and inventory
discrepancies. Discrepancies found should be documented and forwarded through the
Telecommunications Coordinator. OTS NS will review the documentation presented and make
applicable adjustments.
Disputes concerning charges must be directed to the Division of Administration Office of
Finance and Support Services OTS Network Services Support Section at 225 342-0700.
Payment of bill must not be delayed. State agencies must return the mailer page of the invoice
to OTS with payment. Adjustments will not be issued to accounts without proper information
and documentation submitted with remittance. Any questions concerning account balances or
payment should be directed to the General Accounting Unit at 225 342-0700.

Rate Requests
The telecommunications rates for equipment and services are published in the Office of
Technology Services Network Services (OTS NS) Catalog of Services which can be found online
at www.doa.la.gov/Pages/ots/Telecommunications/index.aspx. Inquiries concerning these rates
should be directed to your Telecommunications Coordinator.

Directory Listing Changes
To maintain accurate and current state government listings in both the public telephone
directories and the State Government Telephone Directory, the Office of Technology Services
Network Services must be notified in writing by the agency's Telecommunications Coordinator
of all changes as they occur. The State Government Telephone Directory can be accessed
online at www.doa.la.gov/OTS/OTM/listings/sgtd.pdf.
All requests for directory listings should be submitted by your agency's Telecommunications
Coordinator to the Network Services Information and Training Section at the Office of
Technology Services Network Services, Post Office Box 94280, Baton Rouge, Louisiana 708049280. Detailed instructions pertaining to telephone listings additions, deletions, or changes
should be included. Questions should be directed to the Network Services Information and
Training Section at 225 342-7725.

89

Training
Telecommunications training is available for all state agencies through the Office of
Technology Services Network Services. Instructions on dialing procedures, operation of
various telephone systems and equipment, making the most of your telephone, and proper
utilization of long distance service are some of the subjects for which training is available.
Requests for training should be submitted in writing through your Telecommunications
Coordinator to the Information and Training Section, Office of Technology Services Network
Services, Post Office Box 94280, Baton Rouge, Louisiana 70804-9280. Questions should be
directed to the OTS NS Information and Training Section at 225 342-7725.
